The example also make usage of the ClassPathLoader mechanism i decribed in <a href="http://www.jotschi.de/?p=660">my other post</a>.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-666"></a><br /> I added the jogl2 libraries by using the system scope since i could not find a maven repository with those libraries. The example currently works only with i586 linux. But i could be easily modified to handle other architectures as well.</p> <p>Update: I migrated the nehe jogl examples which i found <a href="http://www.java-tips.org/other-api-tips/jogl/vertex-buffer-objects-nehe-tutorial-jogl-port-2.html">here</a> to make use of jogl2.</p> <p><a href="/images/opengl/JOGLQuadExample.png"><img src="/images/opengl/JOGLQuadExample.png" alt="" title="JOGLQuadExample" width="271" height="283" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-674" /></a></p> JOGL2 (jogamp) ClassPathLoader For Native Libraries 2011-09-26T23:17:02+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2011/09/26/jogl2-jogamp-classpathloader-for-native-libraries <p><strong>Update:</strong><br /> The upcoming RC4 of JOGL2 will support loading of native libraries. I&#8217;ll update this post as soon as i get time to take a look the new loading mechanism.<br /> <br></p> <p>Usually native libraries are loaded by adding the system property java.library.path to the jvm arguments. Its also possible to change the java.library.path within a static block at runtime as described <a href="http://fahdshariff.blogspot.com/2011/08/changing-java-library-path-at-runtime.html">here</a>. It&#8217;s also possible to dynamically load the native libraries at runtime using the System.load method. I just wrote a small ClassPathLoader class that can be handed over to the JNILibLoaderBase class that is dealing with the loading of libraries. <br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-660"></a></p> <p>The ClassPathLoader will allow extraction of the the native libraries from jars that contain all libraries. For jogl2 these jars are jogl-natives-linux-i586.jar and gluegen-rt-natives-linux-i586.jar for linux-i586.</p> <p>This static block can be embedded within your main class. It will disable the default loading mechanism and replace it with the classpath loader. Please note that is required that the native lib jars must be added to the classpath.</p> <pre class="syntax java"> static { ClassPathLoader loader = new ClassPathLoader(); loader.loadLibrary("gluegen-rt", true); JNILibLoaderBase.setLoadingAction(loader); NativeLibLoader.disableLoading(); } </pre> <p>Here is the ClassPathLoader itself. No real magic here as well. Please note that the loader currently only works with linux libraries (<strong>.so). Adaption for windows libraries (</strong>.dll) shouldn&#8217;t be that hard.</p> <pre class="syntax escaped java"> package de.jotschi.jogl2.example; import java.io.File; import java.io.FileOutputStream; import java.io.IOException; import java.io.InputStream; import com.jogamp.common.jvm.JNILibLoaderBase.LoaderAction; public class ClassPathLoader implements LoaderAction { /** * Loads the given library with the libname from the classpath root */ public boolean loadLibrary(String libname, boolean ignoreError) { String filename = &quot;lib&quot; + libname + &quot;.so&quot;; InputStream ins = ClassLoader.getSystemResourceAsStream(filename); try { File tmpFile = writeTmpFile(ins, filename); System.load(tmpFile.getAbsolutePath()); tmpFile.delete(); } catch (IOException e) { e.printStackTrace(); return false; } return true; } /** * Write the content of the inputstream into a tempfile with the given * filename * * @param ins * @param filename * @throws IOException */ private File writeTmpFile(InputStream ins, String filename) throws IOException { File tmpFile = new File(System.getProperty(&quot;java.io.tmpdir&quot;), filename); tmpFile.delete(); FileOutputStream fos = null; try { fos = new FileOutputStream(tmpFile); byte[] buffer = new byte[1024]; int len; while ((len = ins.read(buffer)) != -1) { fos.write(buffer, 0, len); } } finally { if (ins != null) { ins.close(); } if (fos != null) { fos.close(); } } return tmpFile; } public void loadLibrary(String libname, String[] preload, boolean preloadIgnoreError) { loadLibrary(libname, preloadIgnoreError); } } &lt;/pre&gt; </pre> JavaCPP Examples 2011-09-23T21:10:34+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/neuronensturm/technik/2011/09/23/javacpp-examples <p>I finally found the time to write post about the javacpp <a href="https://github.com/Jotschi/javacpp-examples">examples</a> i created since i wanted to explore the capabilities of the <a href="http://code.google.com/p/javacpp/">JavaCPP library</a>.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-645"></a><br /> <em>Please note that the examples are only tested under linux and probably won&#8217;t run on windows/mac.</em><br /> The examples can be fetched from my <a href="https://github.com/Jotschi/javacpp-examples">github repository</a>.<br /> <br/></p> <p>So far i created four different examples. Each for a specific usecase:<br /> <h1>javacpp-sharedlib-example</h1><br /> This example shows how to use a own cpp shared library with the library.</p> <p>The example consists of multiple pieces that finally work together.</p> <h3>1. Cube.cpp</h3> <p>The shared lib will be created from the Cube cpp class.</p> <pre class="syntax c"> #include "Cube.h" void Cube::setSide(double s) { side = s &lt;= 0 ? 1 : s; } double Cube::getSide() { return side; } double Cube::getArea() { return 6 * side * side; } double Cube::getVolume() { return side * side * side; } </pre> <h3>Cube.h</h3> <pre class="syntax c"> #ifndef CUBE_H #define CUBE_H class Cube { private: double side; public: Cube() {}; ~Cube() {}; // copy constructor Cube(class Cube&amp; cube) { side = cube.side; } void setSide(double s); double getSide(); double getArea(); double getVolume(); }; #endif </pre> <h3>2. JavaCube.java</h3> <p>The JavaCube java class acts as a wrapper/glue that fits between the gap of java and native code. Normally you would here defined your jni hooks which then would be implemented. Since i use JavaCPP this step is radically simplified. The annotations are used to give javacpp all the information it needs to prepare its g++ command that in the final compile step will create the library that can be shipped with the java program.</p> <pre class="syntax c"> package de.jotschi.javacpp.example; import static com.googlecode.javacpp.Loader.load; import com.googlecode.javacpp.Pointer; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.Name; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.Platform; @Platform(include = "Cube.h", link = "Cube") public class JavaCube { NativeCube cube; static { load(); } public JavaCube() { cube = new NativeCube(); } public void setSide(double s) { cube.setSide(s); } public double getArea() { return cube.getArea(); } public double getSide() { return cube.getSide(); } public double getVolume() { return cube.getVolume(); } @Name("Cube") public static class NativeCube extends Pointer { static { load(); } public NativeCube() { allocate(); } public NativeCube(Pointer p) { super(p); } public native void setSide(double s); // this = new Cube() private native void allocate(); private native double getArea(); private native double getSide(); private native double getVolume(); } } </pre> <p>Once the java files have been compiled the exec-maven-plugin will be executed which itself executes the makefile that builds the shared library.</p> <pre class="syntax xml"> &lt;execution&gt; &lt;id&gt;build-sharedlib&lt;/id&gt; &lt;phase&gt;process-classes&lt;/phase&gt; &lt;goals&gt; &lt;goal&gt;exec&lt;/goal&gt; &lt;/goals&gt; &lt;configuration&gt; &lt;executable&gt;make&lt;/executable&gt; &lt;commandlineArgs&gt;main&lt;/commandlineArgs&gt; &lt;workingDirectory&gt;${basedir}/src/main/jni&lt;/workingDirectory&gt; &lt;/configuration&gt; &lt;/execution&gt; </pre> <p>This library will be used within the next execution of the exec-maven-plugin. This final execution step will invoke the javacpp builder which generated the jni headers from the java class annotations and it also compiles the jni header interface against the previously created library.</p> <pre class="syntax xml"> &lt;execution&gt; &lt;id&gt;build-jnilib&lt;/id&gt; &lt;phase&gt;process-classes&lt;/phase&gt; &lt;goals&gt; &lt;goal&gt;exec&lt;/goal&gt; &lt;/goals&gt; &lt;configuration&gt; &lt;executable&gt;java&lt;/executable&gt; &lt;commandlineArgs&gt;-jar ../libs/javacpp.jar -Dcompiler.linkpath=${basedir}/target/classes/linux-x86 -Dcompiler.includepath=${basedir}/src/main/jni -classpath target/classes de.jotschi.javacpp.example.JavaCube&lt;/commandlineArgs&gt; &lt;/configuration&gt; &lt;/execution&gt; </pre> <p>The CubeTest.java Junit tests shows how the created java class that wraps the native class works.</p> <h1>javacpp-libc6-example / javacpp-stdlib-example</h1> <p>These examples are very similar to the javacpp-sharedlib-example. The libc6 example show how to use JavaCPP with the libc6 library and c code. The stdlib example on the other hand uses the c++ stdlib.</p> <h1>javacpp-android-example</h1> <p>This example shows how to use a android maven project in combination with JavaCPP. The example shows how to mix java with native code. The java part creates a opengl surface and the native code is used to execute a opengl function that changed the color of the display.</p> Where words are only half the story.. 2011-09-23T02:17:56+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/fundgrube/2011/09/23/audiobooks-mixed-with-soundtracks <p>Classic audiobooks combined with ambient chilling trance soundtracks by <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Oakenfold">Paul Oakenfold</a> became the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_Soundtracks">Urban Soundtracks</a> which can be found <a href="http://www.pauloakenfold.com/forum/genera/51868">here</a>.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-640"></a><br /> A similar dubstep track by <a href="http://erwt.blogspot.com/">erwtenpeller aka Niels Jansen</a> can be found <a href="http://soundcloud.com/erwtenpeller/war-of-the-worlds">here</a>.</p> NasaTV HD Linux 2011-09-03T16:07:26+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2011/09/03/nasatv-hd-linux <p>I just found a very useful script to download the Nasatv HD stream on linux. The script was written by the user Naito. I found it <a href="http://forum.nasaspaceflight.com/index.php?topic=19846.990;wap2">here</a><a id="more"></a><a id="more-632"></a></p> <pre class="syntax c"> #!/bin/bash filename="NASA-TV-HD.`date +%y%m%d-%s`" httpurl='http://liveips.nasa.gov.edgesuite.net/msfc/Wifi.m3u8' trap "break; echo Finished recording. ; exit 0" SIGINT SIGTERM echo -n Buffering #Get initial set of files for nextfile in $(curl -s $httpurl | grep '.ts'); do echo -n . curl -s "$nextfile" &gt;&gt; $filename.ts lastfile="$nextfile" done echo 100\% echo Starting continuous recording. Press CTRL-C to quit. while true; do nextfile=$(curl -s $httpurl | grep '.ts' | tail -1) if [ "$nextfile" != "$lastfile" ]; then curl -s "$nextfile" &gt;&gt; $filename.ts lastfile="$nextfile" fi #File list updates every 10 seconds, but don't want to sleep too long and miss an update! sleep 7 done </pre> JNI via JavaCPP on Android 2011-08-25T23:50:55+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2011/08/25/jni-via-javacpp-on-android <p>There are multiple ways to get <span class="caps">JNI</span> working with android. You can of course do it the manual way and create header file and includes in your java classes but thats a lot of work and it might be even prone to errors. <a href="http://www.koushikdutta.com/2009/01/jni-in-android-and-foreword-of-why-jni.html">Here is a good post</a> from Koushik Dutta that summarizes those bad parts in detail. This post will focus on getting started with JavaCPP and Android.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-624"></a><br /> There are some approaches to get rid of all those manual steps. There is for example <a href="https://github.com/twall/jna"><span class="caps">JNA</span> (Java Native Access)</a>. <a href="http://www.ok.ctrl.titech.ac.jp/~saudet/">Aamuel Audet</a> the author of JavaCPP wrote a patch for <span class="caps">JNA</span> to support Android. But <span class="caps">JNA</span> has also some <a href="http://codeanticode.wordpress.com/2010/12/07/jna-on-android/">problems</a> and <a href="https://github.com/twall/jna/blob/master/www/FrequentlyAskedQuestions.md"> drawbacks</a> which should be noted.</p> <p>Another solution is using JavaCPP by Aamuel Audet. This post will describe how to get JavaCPP working with Android.</p> <h3>Create an Eclipse Android project</h3> <p>Use the wizard and create a new android project with the name NativeTest.</p> <h3>Add JavaCPP to the project libs</h3> <p>Download the javacpp binary archive and place the javacpp.jar into the /libs folder of your project. Create the folder if it does not exist. Add the javacpp.jar to your buildpath</p> <h3>Add JavaCPP example code to your project</h3> <p>Replace your default activity class with the content of NativeTestActivity. You need to adapt some package names.</p> <p>The example is very simple and was fetched from the JavaCPP tutorial page but i guess it shows really good how to get started with JavaCPP. If the app does not crash you&#8217;ll know for sure that everything is fine.</p> <pre class="syntax java"> package de.jotschi; import com.googlecode.javacpp.Loader; import com.googlecode.javacpp.Pointer; import com.googlecode.javacpp.PointerPointer; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.ByRef; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.Cast; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.Name; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.Namespace; import com.googlecode.javacpp.annotation.Platform; import android.app.Activity; import android.os.Bundle; @Platform(include = "&lt;vector&gt;") @Namespace("std") public class NativeTestActivity extends Activity { static { Loader.load(); } /** Called when the activity is first created. */ @Override public void onCreate(Bundle savedInstanceState) { super.onCreate(savedInstanceState); setContentView(R.layout.main); PointerVector v = new PointerVector(42); Pointer p = new Pointer() { { address = 0xDEADBEEFL; } }; v.get(0).put(p); PointerVector v2 = new PointerVector().copy(v); Pointer p2 = v2.at(0).get(); System.out.println(v2.size() + " " + p2); } @Name("vector&lt;void*&gt;") public static class PointerVector extends Pointer { public PointerVector() { allocate(); } public PointerVector(long n) { allocate(n); } public PointerVector(Pointer p) { super(p); } // this = (vector&lt;void*&gt;*)p private native void allocate(); // this = new std::vector&lt;void*&gt;() private native void allocate(long n); // this = new // std::vector&lt;void*&gt;(n) @Name("operator=") public native @ByRef PointerVector copy(@ByRef PointerVector x); public native long size(); public native @Cast("bool") boolean empty(); @Name("operator[]") public native @ByRef PointerPointer get(long n); public native @ByRef PointerPointer at(long n); } } </pre> <h3>Create the native files using JavaCPP</h3> <p>Switch into your workspace directory and execute the following command. Please note that you have to change your paths accordingly.</p> <pre class="syntax c"> jotschi@Amilo:~/workspace/NativeTest$ java -jar libs/javacpp.jar -classpath bin/ -d libs/armeabi/ -properties android-arm -Dplatform.root=/opt/ide/android-ndk-r6 -Dcompiler.path=/opt/ide/android-ndk-r6/toolchains/arm-linux-androideabi-4.4.3/prebuilt/linux-x86/bin/arm-linux-androideabi-g++ -classpath /opt/ide/android-sdk-linux_x86/platforms/android-10/android.jar de.jotschi.NativeTestActivity </pre> <p>You can also create an external builder task to execute the generation process automatically. This <a href="http://mobilepearls.com/labs/ndk-builder-in-eclipse/">post</a> describes how to setup a builder for the ndk.</p> <h3>Execute the example</h3> <p>Now you can execute the example on your android device. Please note that enabling &#8216;debug&#8217; within your android manifest will help debugging. LogCat will only print stacktraces if you have enabled that option.</p> Eclipse CDT Cross Platform Development Within A Chroot Environment 2011-07-08T18:36:49+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/2011/07/08/eclipse-cdt-cross-platform-development-within-a-chroot-environment <p>This post is about how to configure eclipse to work with a chroot environment that is setup for cross compiling against <span class="caps">ARM</span> architecture.</p> <p>Please refer to my post <a href="/?p=594">Cross Compile Pandaboard PowerVR OpenGL ES2 Example</a> if you want to know how to setup a chroot environment for cross compiling. <br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-615"></a></p> <h3>1. Install sudo and configure sudo</h3> <p>Install sudo:</p> <pre class="syntax c"> apt-get install sudo </pre> <p>Allow every user that is within the sudo group to execute the chroot command without entering a password by adding the line to /etc/sudoers:</p> <pre class="syntax c" title="/etc/sudoers"> %sudo ALL= NOPASSWD: /usr/sbin/chroot </pre> <h3>2. Prepare the project</h3> <p>The project must be located within the within the chroot environment. You could use bind mounts to create a mountpoint that connects your workspace project with a folder inside the chroot enviroment. I just placed the project itself inside the chroot environment and created a symlink that points to my workspace. Keep in mind to close your project or eclipse if you move the project files outside of eclipse.</p> <ul> <li>1. Create your <span class="caps">CDT</span> project.</li> <li>2. Close the project within eclipse.</li> <li>3. Move the project directory from e.g.: ~/workspace/MyProject/ to ~/mychroot/opt/MyProject</li> <li>4. Create a symlink inside of ~/workspace with the name <i>MyProject</i> that points to ~/mychroot/opt/MyProject<br /> <li>5. Open the project within eclipse</li> </ul> <h3>3. Create a external build script</h3> <p>This example script (e.g: ~/workspace/MyProject/compile.sh) will execute the bash command inside of the chroot environment which is located at $<span class="caps">HOME</span>/mychroot. The bash command will switch into the project location inside the chroot environment and execute make. Of course you can optimize the script to make it more generic and so on. But for now i&#8217;ll keep it simple.</p> <pre class="syntax c"> #!/bin/bash sudo chroot $HOME/mychroot/ bash -c 'cd /opt/MyProject/; make clean; make' </pre> <h3>4. Configure your eclipse cdt project</h3> <p>Now we have to change the builder for our project. Since we don&#8217;t want to use the host environment to build the project we need to tell eclipse to use our compile.sh script which we created earlier. Go into <i>project properties &#8594; C/C++ Build &#8594; Builder Settings</i> and select <strong>External builder</strong>. Point the Build command to your compile.sh.</p> <p>To fix syntax errors within your project you have to add the correct includes of course. Go to <i>project properties &#8594; C/C++ Build &#8594; Setting &#8594; Tool Settings</i> and add the include directories from your chroot enviroment. If you are using xapt to install cross libraries please note that those files are usually located at <strong>/usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/</strong>.</p> <p>Example for libx11-dev</p> <pre class="syntax c"> root@NeXuS:/# dpkg -L libx11-dev-armel-cross /. /usr /usr/share /usr/share/doc /usr/share/doc/libx11-dev-armel-cross /usr/share/doc/libx11-dev-armel-cross/README /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11 /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xregion.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xresource.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xlib.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/cursorfont.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/XKBlib.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xlibint.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xutil.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/XlibConf.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/ImUtil.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xlocale.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/include/X11/Xcms.h /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/lib /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/lib/pkgconfig /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/lib/pkgconfig/x11.pc /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/lib/libX11.a /usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/lib/libX11.so </pre> Cross a very simple OpenGL ES2 example for the Pandaboard within a Debian Linux chroot environment.</p> <p><a id="more"></a><a id="more-594"></a></p> <p><strong>What do we need?</strong><br /> <i><br /> Get cross compile dependencies</h3> <pre class="syntax c"> xapt -m -a armel libx11-dev xapt -m -a armel libdrm-dev </pre> <h3>6. Extract the example and compile</h3> <h4><a href="/downloads/PandaboardPowerVROGLES2Example.tgz">Download</a> the example</h4> <pre class="syntax c"> cd /opt/ wget http://www.jotschi.de/downloads/PandaboardPowerVROGLES2Example.tgz tar xvfz PandaboardPowerVROGLES2Example.tgz </pre> <h4>Store Settings<br /> Contents of /opt/settings.inc</h4> <pre class="syntax c"> #!/bin/bash export X11ROOT=/usr/arm-linux-gnueabi/ export PVR_OMAP_FILES=/opt/pvr-omap4-1.7.5.2+git20110610+9696932c.2 </pre> <h4>Load settings and compile:</h4> <pre class="syntax c"> cd /opt/OGLES2PowerVRPandaboardExample # If . does not work use source to include the settings . /opt/settings.inc # Invoke the build make </pre> <h3>Optional for pandaboard cross platform development</h3> <p>Now i have a build arm ready binary executable within my chroot environment. To execute it straight from eclipse we have to create another script. The script will transfer our executable (in this case OGLES2HelloTriangle) to the Pandaboard OMAP4 platform and execute it there.</p> <p><i>run.sh:</i></p> <pre class="syntax c"> #!/bin/bash echo "Transfering" scp ReleaseX11/OGLES2HelloTriangle root@panda:/opt/ echo "Executing" ssh root@panda DISPLAY=:0 /opt/OGLES2HelloTriangle </pre> <p>Just create a new C/C++ Application run configuration that uses the following settings:<br /> <ul><br /> <li>C/C++ Application: /bin/bash</li><br /> <li>Program arguments: /home/myuser/workspace/MyProject/run.sh</li></p> </ul> Pandaboard OpenGL PowerVR CrossCompile On Debian 2011-07-07T00:45:28+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2011/07/07/pandaboard-opengl-powervr-crosscompile-on-debian <p>This post is about how to compile the PowerVR <span class="caps">SDK</span> Examples within a Debian Linux Chroot environment. You don&#8217;t need to install a custom/patched Kernel for <span class="caps">LXC</span> since the support is included within the Kernel Mainline. As for Debian Linux VServers support will be dropped in future releases. This means <span class="caps">LXC</span> is the way to go. Okay enough talking. Lets get to work.<a id="more"></a><a id="more-554"></a></p> <h2>Setup:</h2> <p>1. Install Linux Containers<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> apt-get install lxc </pre></p> <p>2. Add cgroup mount point:<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> mkdir -p /var/local/cgroup echo &quot;cgroup /var/local/cgroup cgroup defaults 0 0&quot; &gt;&gt; /etc/fstab mount -a </pre></p> <p>3. Install bridge utils<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> apt-get install bridge-utils </pre></p> <p>4. Convert your eth0 configuration into a br0 bridge configuration:<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"></p> <ol> <li>The primary network interface<br /> #auto eth0<br /> #allow-hotplug eth0<br /> #iface eth0 inet static<br /> #address 192.168.10.1<br /> #netmask 255.255.255.0</li> </ol> <p>auto br0<br /> iface br0 inet static<br /> bridge_ports eth0<br /> bridge_fd 0<br /> address 192.168.10.1<br /> netmask 255.255.255.0<br /> </pre></notextile><br /> Please keep in mind that this change might also affect your firewall settings and/or other connections.</p> <p>5. Enable IP forwarding<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> echo 1 &gt; /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_forward </pre></p> <p>6. Create a new container.<br /> I used a modified version of the lxc-debian template script from Daniel Lezcano which is included in the <span class="caps">LXC</span> debian package. It can be found here /usr/lib/lxc/templates/lxc-debian. The modfied version can be downloaded <a href="/downloads/lxc/lxc-debian">here</a>.<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> wget http://www.jotschi.de/downloads/lxc/lxc-debian chmod +x lxc-debian ./lxc-debian ./lxc-debian squeeze test 2 </pre><br /> Your container with the name test will be installed at /var/lib/lxc/test.</p> <p>7. Adapt container network configuration<br /> For my configuration i had to adapt the resolv.conf and the /etc/network/interfaces file.<br /> I changed the nameserver to 192.168.10.1 since my nameserver is running of that ip.<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> nameserver 192.168.10.1 </pre></p> <p>I also adapted the container /etc/network/interfaces file.<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> auto eth0 iface eth0 inet static address 192.168.10.26 netmask 255.255.255.0 gateway 192.168.10.1 </pre></p> <p>You can edit those file outside of your conainer by editing:<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> /var/lib/lxc/test/rootfs/etc/network/interfaces /var/lib/lxc/test/rootfs/etc/resolv.conf </pre></p> <p>8. Start the container<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> lxc-start -n test -d </pre></p> <p>9. Enter the conainer<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> lxc-console -n test </pre></p> <p>The default login is root/root.</p> <p><br/> Use this manual for migrating linux vservers to lxc:<br /> <a href="http://schmidi2.blog.com/2010/10/25/migrating-from-vserver-to-lxc/">migrating-from-vserver-to-lxc</a></p> Pandaboard Audiosetup 2011-07-01T20:47:55+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2011/07/01/pandaboard-audiosetup <p>To get audio with the pandaboard working all you need is the following commands. At the creation of the QuadTree the start coordinates and the bounds of the tree must be specified.</p> <p>RenderPointQuadTree.java is an executable application that shows how to work with the QuadTree data. Leftclick will insert a new point. Rightclick will highlight the elements within the identified cell/node. <br /> <a href="/images/quadtree/quadtree.png"><img src="/images/quadtree/quadtree.png" alt="RenderQuadTree" title="quadtree" width="590" height="570" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-531" /></a></p> <p>RenderSpatialQuadTree.java is an executable application that show how to use the spatial QuadTree implementation. In this case the quadtree will be used to store some images. The QuadTree has a specific dimension (512&#215;512 in this case). We just add a buch of different images which have different sizes. Everything is contained within a single jar.</p> <p><a id="more"></a><a id="more-519"></a></p> <p>Insipred by <a href="http://open.bekk.no/2011/01/14/embedded-jetty-7-webapp-executable-with-maven/">this blogpost</a> ( <a href="https://github.com/bekkopen/jetty-pkg">Code</a> ) i created a similar example using maven which you can find here: <a href="https://github.com/Jotschi/Uberjar-Dummy-Webapp">Example Sources</a>.</p> <p>It contains a uberjar webapp that will be served using jetty. The idea behind this feature is that some applications allocate large amounts of memory just in case, but never actually use it. Thus, memory overcommit allows you to run more applications than actually fit in your memory, provided the applications don&#8217;t actually use the memory they have allocated. If they do, then the kernel terminates the application.</p> </p> <p> <a href="http://www.Jotschi.de/?p=512#more-512" class="more-link"><span class="read-on">read on</span></a></p> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> #include &lt;stdio.h&gt; #include &lt;stdlib.h&gt; #include &lt;string.h&gt; #include &lt;unistd.h&gt; main() { int i; for(i=0;i&lt;9000;i++) { int *ptr = malloc(i*1024*1024); if (ptr == NULL) { printf (&quot;Soft memory allocation failed for %i MB\n&quot;,i ); break; } else { free(ptr); ptr = NULL; } } for(i=0;i&lt;9000;i++) { int *ptr = malloc(i*1024*1024); if (ptr == NULL) { printf (&quot;Memory allocation failed for %i MB\n&quot;,i ); break; } else { memset(ptr, 0, i*1024*1024); printf(&quot;Wrote %i MB to memory\n&quot;, i); //usleep(1000); free(ptr); ptr = NULL; } } } </pre> XServer within VServer Linux 2010-10-15T18:11:50+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2010/10/15/xserver-within-vserver-linux <p>There multiple ways to use X within a vserver. The most common would be a remote connected x session. If you just want to connect to your vserver guest and join a remote session you just need to install the desktop manager that you want to use and additionally you will need a remote control software. I prefer <a href="http://www.nomachine.com/select-package.php?os=linux&id=1">Nomachine FreeNX</a> because it is very fast and versatile.</p> <p>The other way to use a X server within a vserver is the non remote version with direct usage of video hardware of the host computer.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-505"></a></p> <p>1. Set capabilities for the vserver guest. (Perhaps only SYS_RAWIO is needed)<br /> <pre class="syntax bash"><br /> echo -e &#8220;SYS_RAWIO\nIPC_LOCK\nIPC_OWNER\nSYS_RAWIO\nSYS_ADMIN\nNET_ADMIN\nNET_RAW\nMKNOD&#8221; &gt; /etc/vservers/desktop-guest/bcapabilities<br /> </pre></p> <p>2. Create needed device nodes for the guest by coping nodes in the host system<br /> <pre class="syntax bash"><br /> cp -ax /dev/tty7 /var/lib/vservers/dev/<br /> cd /var/lib/vservers/desktop-guest/dev/<br /> ln -s tty7 tty0<br /> cp -ax /dev/nvidiactl /var/lib/vservers/desktop-guest/dev/<br /> cp -ax /dev/nvidia0 /var/lib/vservers/desktop-guest/dev/<br /> </pre></p> <p>3. Install the <span class="caps">NVIDIA</span> drivers within the guest without the kernel module. The driver must be installed within the host system as well in order to provide the loaded kernel module. <br /> <pre class="syntax bash"><br /> ./<span class="caps">NVIDIA</span>-Linux-x86-256.53.run &#8212;no-kernel-module<br /> </pre></p> <p>4. Mount sysfs within the guest:<br /> <pre class="syntax bash"><br /> mount -t sysfs /sys /sys<br /> </pre></p> <p>5. Finally you can start the xserver within the guest:<br /> <pre class="syntax bash"><br /> startx &#8212; :0 vt7 -br -novtswitch -sharevts -dpi 100 -nolisten tcp<br /> </pre></p> <p>This was tested using:<br /> Host: Debian lenny<br /> Guest: Debian squeeze</p> <p>Additional hints:</p> <p>If you want audio support just install alsa within the guest:<br /> <pre class="syntax bash">apt-get install alsa</pre></p> <p>And copy the /dev/snd directory from the host to the guest:<br /> <pre class="syntax bash"><br /> mv /var/lib/vservers/desktop-guest/dev /tmp<br /> cp -rax /dev/snd /var/lib/vservers/desktop-guest/dev/<br /> </pre></p> Summarize memory consumption for linux processes 2010-09-08T12:44:36+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2010/09/08/summarize-memory-consumption-for-linux-processes <p>This script will summarize the memory consuption for a given pattern. It will filter all process args by this pattern and summarize the memory consumption.</p> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> #!/bin/bash a=0 sum=0 for entry in `ps -eo rss,args | grep $1 | sed &quot;s/\s.*//&quot;` ; do a=$(($a+1)); sum=$(($sum+$entry)); done #echo $a; echo &quot;Found: $a processes - Memory Usage: $sum - $(($sum/1024))&quot; </pre> Aloha Editor Wordpress Plugin 2010-09-01T22:42:45+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2010/09/01/aloha-editor-wordpress-plugin <h2>About:</h2> <p>This is a Wordpress Plugin which enables editing of posts by the usage of <a href="http://www.aloha-editor.org/">Aloha Editor</a>.<br></p><p>This Project was discontinued. I could not get sockets working properly. After some googling i figured out that it had to be a network configuration issue.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-480"></a><br /> By default (Debian Testing) sockets bind only to ipv6.</p> <p>The socket binding behaviour can be configured within:</p> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> cat /etc/sysctl.d/bindv6only.conf Set the parameter from net.ipv6.bindv6only=1 to net.ipv6.bindv6only=0 </pre><p>To test the setting you can also use the following command:<br /> <blockquote>sysctl -w net.ipv6.bindv6only=0</blockquote></p> <p>The error messages might be:<br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> Caused by: java.net.SocketException: Network is unreachable at java.net.PlainSocketImpl.socketConnect(Native Method) at java.net.PlainSocketImpl.doConnect(PlainSocketImpl.java:333) at java.net.PlainSocketImpl.connectToAddress(PlainSocketImpl.java:195) at java.net.PlainSocketImpl.connect(PlainSocketImpl.java:182) at java.net.SocksSocketImpl.connect(SocksSocketImpl.java:366) at java.net.Socket.connect(Socket.java:525) </pre></p> <p>Or for debugging java:</p> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> FATAL ERROR in native method: JDWP No transports initialized, jvmtiError=AGENT_ERROR_TRANSPORT_INIT(197) ERROR: transport error 202: connect failed: Connection refused ERROR: JDWP Transport dt_socket failed to initialize, TRANSPORT_INIT(510) JDWP exit error AGENT_ERROR_TRANSPORT_INIT(197): No transports initialized [../../../src/share/back/debugInit.c:690] </pre> OpenGL Tesselation Techniques Comparison 2009-12-16T01:22:24+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/gfx/2009/12/16/opengl-tesselation-techniques-comparison <p>There is a veraity of different tesselation techniques you can use within opengl. This post should give a overview over the different techniques currently available:<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-471"></a></p> <p><iframe width="560" height="420" src="http://www.youtube.com/embed/Bcalc8UoJzo?color=white&theme=light"></iframe></p> <ul> <p><br/> <strong>1. External Library:</strong><br /> <a href="http://www.cs.cmu.edu/~quake/triangle.html">Triangle</a></p> <li>Pro&#8217;s: More flexibel usage</li> <li>Con&#8217;s: Doesn&#8217;t use <span class="caps">GPU</span> computing capabilities</li> <p><br/></p> <p><strong>2. Static pipeline functionality provided by <span class="caps">GLU</span> the GLUtesselator:</strong></p> <p><a href="/?p=466">OpenGL <span class="caps">GLU</span> Tesselation Method Without DisplayLists</a></p> <li>Pro&#8217;s: Simple to use</li> <li>Con&#8217;s: Doesn&#8217;t use <span class="caps">GPU</span> computing capabilities</li> <p><br/> <strong>3. Using the GL_AMD_vertex_shader_tessellator extension from <span class="caps">AMD</span> / <span class="caps">ATI</span></strong></p> <p><a href="http://www.opengl.org/registry/specs/AMD/vertex_shader_tessellator.txt">Spec: vertex_shader_tessellator</a><br /> <a href="/?p=460">OpenGL <span class="caps">AMD</span> Tesselation Example (CatmullCark SubDivision) &#8211; Linux</a></p> <li>Pro&#8217;s: Does use <span class="caps">GPU</span> computing features</li> <li>Con&#8217;s: Does not work with Nvidia cards at all.</li> <p><br/> <strong>4. Using OpenGL 3.2 Geometry Shader Extensions:</strong></p> <p><a href="http://www.opengl.org/registry/specs/EXT/geometry_shader4.txt">Spec: geometry_shader4</a><br /> <a href="http://wiki.delphigl.com/index.php/shader_tesselation">http://wiki.delphigl.com/index.php/shader_tesselation</a></p> <li>Pro&#8217;s: Does use <span class="caps">GPU</span> computing features</li> <li>Con&#8217;s: <span class="caps">GPU</span> must Shader Model 4</li> </ul> OpenGL GLU Tesselation Method Without DisplayLists 2009-12-15T23:23:32+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/gfx/2009/12/15/opengl-glu-tesselation-method-without-displaylists <p>Due to the deprecation of &#8216;DisplayLists&#8217; within OpenGL 3.2 i wanted to store my tessellated mesh within a structure which i could use later on. Therefor it is possible to use the GLU_TESS_VERTEX_DATA, GLU_TESS_BEGIN_DATA etc gluTessCallback hooks.</p> <p>When calling the gluTessBeginPolygon method it is possible to pass a address to a own structure along as second argument. This address will be handled to the callback methods and therefor you can access your defined data structure to store the tessellated data within it. My example shows how to deal with that. <br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-466"></a><br /> I use the <a href="http://glm.g-truc.net/about.html">OpenGL Mathematics Library</a> to handle my points.</p> <p><img src="/images/tesselation/tesselation_star.png" alt="tesselation_star" title="tesselation_star" width="240" height="216" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-468" /></p> <p><img src="/images/tesselation/tesselation_star_wire.png" alt="tesselation_star_wire" title="tesselation_star_wire" width="232" height="205" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-469" /></p> <p><strong>GL_GLUT_TesselationData.cpp</strong></p> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> #include &lt;GL/glut.h&gt; #include &lt;stdlib.h&gt; #include &lt;stdio.h&gt; #include &lt;vector&gt; #include &quot;glm/glm.hpp&quot; using namespace std; //#define USEDISPLAYLIST GLuint startList; GLdouble **dataOutFinal; #ifndef USEDISPLAYLIST struct Mesh { std::vector&lt;glm::vec3&gt; points; GLenum type; } mesh; #endif GLdouble rect[4][3] = { 50.0, 50.0, 0.0, 200.0, 50.0, 0.0, 200.0, 140.0, 0.0, 50.0, 200.0, 0.0 }; GLdouble star[5][6] = { 250.0, 50.0, 0.0, 1.0, 0.0, 1.0, 325.0, 200.0, 0.0, 1.0, 1.0, 0.0, 400.0, 50.0, 0.0, 0.0, 1.0, 1.0, 250.0, 150.0, 0.0, 1.0, 0.0, 0.0, 400.0, 150.0, 0.0, 0.0, 1.0, 0.0 }; void display(void) { glClear(GL_COLOR_BUFFER_BIT); glColor3f(1.0, 0.5, 1.0); // Enable this to see the wireframe //glPolygonMode(GL_FRONT_AND_BACK, GL_LINE); #ifndef USEDISPLAYLIST vector&lt;glm::vec3&gt;::const_iterator cii; glBegin(mesh.type); for (cii = mesh.points.begin(); cii != mesh.points.end(); cii++) { glVertex3f((*cii).x, (*cii).y, (*cii).z); printf(&quot;Result: %f,%f,%f\n&quot;, (*cii).x, (*cii).y, (*cii).z); } glEnd(); #else glCallList(startList); #endif glFlush(); } void beginCallback(GLenum which, void *resultMesh) { printf(&quot;Type: %i\n&quot;, which); #ifdef USEDISPLAYLIST glBegin(which); #else Mesh *myMesh = (Mesh*) resultMesh; (*myMesh).type = which; #endif } void errorCallback(GLenum errorCode) { const GLubyte *estring; estring = gluErrorString(errorCode); fprintf(stderr, &quot;Tessellation Error: %s\n&quot;, estring); exit(0); } void endCallback(void *tessellationSetAddress) { #ifdef USEDISPLAYLIST glEnd(); #endif } void vertexCallback(GLvoid *data, void *resultMesh) { const GLdouble *pointer; pointer = (GLdouble *) data; #ifdef USEDISPLAYLIST glColor3dv(pointer + 3); glVertex3dv(pointer); #else Mesh *myMesh = (Mesh*) resultMesh; (*myMesh).points.push_back(glm::vec3(pointer[0], pointer[1], pointer[2])); #endif printf(&quot;Added new vertex[%f][%f][%f]\n&quot;, pointer[0], pointer[1], pointer[2]); } void combineCallback(GLdouble coords[3], GLdouble *vertex_data[4], GLfloat weight[4], GLdouble **dataOut, void *resultMesh) { GLdouble *vertex; vertex = (GLdouble *) malloc(6 * sizeof(GLdouble)); vertex[0] = coords[0]; vertex[1] = coords[1]; vertex[2] = coords[2]; #ifndef USEDISPLAYLIST Mesh *myMesh = (Mesh*) resultMesh; (*myMesh).points.push_back(glm::vec3(vertex[0], vertex[1], vertex[2])); #endif printf(&quot;Added combine vertex[%f][%f][%f]\n&quot;, vertex[0], vertex[1], vertex[2]); *dataOut = vertex; } void init(void) { GLUtesselator *tobj; glClearColor(0.0, 0.0, 0.0, 0.0); tobj = gluNewTess(); gluTessCallback(tobj, GLU_TESS_VERTEX_DATA, (void(*)()) vertexCallback); gluTessCallback(tobj, GLU_TESS_BEGIN_DATA, (void(*)()) beginCallback); gluTessCallback(tobj, GLU_TESS_END_DATA, (void(*)()) endCallback); gluTessCallback(tobj, GLU_TESS_ERROR, (void(*)()) errorCallback); gluTessCallback(tobj, GLU_TESS_COMBINE_DATA, (void(*)()) combineCallback); #ifdef USEDISPLAYLIST startList = glGenLists(1); glNewList(startList, GL_COMPILE); #endif glShadeModel(GL_SMOOTH); gluTessProperty(tobj, GLU_TESS_WINDING_RULE, GLU_TESS_WINDING_POSITIVE); #ifdef USEDISPLAYLIST gluTessBeginPolygon(tobj, NULL); #else gluTessBeginPolygon(tobj, &amp;mesh); #endif /* gluTessBeginContour(tobj); gluTessVertex(tobj, rect[0], rect[0]); gluTessVertex(tobj, rect[1], rect[1]); gluTessVertex(tobj, rect[2], rect[2]); gluTessVertex(tobj, rect[3], rect[3]); gluTessEndContour(tobj); */ gluTessBeginContour(tobj); gluTessVertex(tobj, star[0], star[0]); gluTessVertex(tobj, star[1], star[1]); gluTessVertex(tobj, star[2], star[2]); gluTessVertex(tobj, star[3], star[3]); gluTessVertex(tobj, star[4], star[4]); gluTessEndContour(tobj); gluTessEndPolygon(tobj); #ifdef USEDISPLAYLIST glEndList(); #endif gluDeleteTess(tobj); printf(&quot;Done\n&quot;); } void reshape(int w, int h) { glViewport(0, 0, (GLsizei) w, (GLsizei) h); glMatrixMode(GL_PROJECTION); glLoadIdentity(); gluOrtho2D(0.0, (GLdouble) w, 0.0, (GLdouble) h); } void keyboard(unsigned char key, int x, int y) { switch (key) { case 27: exit(0); break; } } int main(int argc, char** argv) { glutInit(&amp;argc, argv); glutInitDisplayMode(GLUT_SINGLE | GLUT_RGB); glutInitWindowSize(500, 500); glutCreateWindow(argv[0]); init(); glutDisplayFunc(display); glutReshapeFunc(reshape); glutKeyboardFunc(keyboard); glutMainLoop(); return 0; } </pre> OpenGL AMD Tesselation Example (CatmullCark SubDivision) - Linux 2009-12-15T02:22:53+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/2009/12/15/opengl-amd-tesselation-example-catmullcark-subdivision-linux <p>While searching for a tesselation example i stumbled uppon this example. Extract the two important matrices you wish to visualize:<br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> static float proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr16"><a href="#fn16">16</a></sup>;<br /> glGetFloatv(GL_PROJECTION_MATRIX, proj);</p> <p>static float mv<sup class="footnote" id="fnr16"><a href="#fn16">16</a></sup>;<br /> glGetFloatv(GL_MODELVIEW_MATRIX, mv);<br /> </pre></p> <p>2. Do some math and draw your frustum:<br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> void Helper::drawFrustum(float * proj, float *mv) {</p> <p>// Get near and far from the Projection matrix.<br /> const double near = proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr11"><a href="#fn11">11</a></sup> / (proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr10"><a href="#fn10">10</a></sup> &#8211; 1.0);<br /> const double far = proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr11"><a href="#fn11">11</a></sup> / (1.0 + proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr10"><a href="#fn10">10</a></sup>);</p> <p>// Get the sides of the near plane.<br /> const double nLeft = near * (proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr2"><a href="#fn2">2</a></sup> &#8211; 1.0) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr0"><a href="#fn0">0</a></sup>;<br /> const double nRight = near * (1.0 + proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr2"><a href="#fn2">2</a></sup>) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr0"><a href="#fn0">0</a></sup>;<br /> const double nTop = near * (1.0 + proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr6"><a href="#fn6">6</a></sup>) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr5"><a href="#fn5">5</a></sup>;<br /> const double nBottom = near * (proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr6"><a href="#fn6">6</a></sup> &#8211; 1.0) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr5"><a href="#fn5">5</a></sup>;</p> <p>// Get the sides of the far plane.<br /> const double fLeft = far * (proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr2"><a href="#fn2">2</a></sup> &#8211; 1.0) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr0"><a href="#fn0">0</a></sup>;<br /> const double fRight = far * (1.0 + proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr2"><a href="#fn2">2</a></sup>) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr0"><a href="#fn0">0</a></sup>;<br /> const double fTop = far * (1.0 + proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr6"><a href="#fn6">6</a></sup>) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr5"><a href="#fn5">5</a></sup>;<br /> const double fBottom = far * (proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr6"><a href="#fn6">6</a></sup> &#8211; 1.0) / proj<sup class="footnote" id="fnr5"><a href="#fn5">5</a></sup>;</p> <p>/*<br /> 0 glVertex3f(0.0f, 0.0f, 0.0f);<br /> 1 glVertex3f(nLeft, nBottom, -near);<br /> 2 glVertex3f(nRight, nBottom, -near);<br /> 3 glVertex3f(nRight, nTop, -near);<br /> 4 glVertex3f(nLeft, nTop, -near);<br /> 5 glVertex3f(fLeft, fBottom, -far);<br /> 6 glVertex3f(fRight, fBottom, -far);<br /> 7 glVertex3f(fRight, fTop, -far);<br /> 8 glVertex3f(fLeft, fTop, -far);<br /> */</p> <p>glMatrixMode(GL_MODELVIEW);<br /> glPushMatrix();<br /> //glLoadIdentity ();</p> // <span class="caps">TODO</span> &#8211; Update: You need to invert the mv before multiplying it with the current mv! <p>glMultMatrixf(mv);</p> <p>glLineWidth(2);<br /> glBegin(GL_LINES);</p> <p>glVertex3f(0.0f, 0.0f, 0.0f);<br /> glVertex3f(fLeft, fBottom, -far);</p> <p>glVertex3f(0.0f, 0.0f, 0.0f);<br /> glVertex3f(fRight, fBottom, -far);</p> <p>glVertex3f(0.0f, 0.0f, 0.0f);<br /> glVertex3f(fRight, fTop, -far);</p> <p>glVertex3f(0.0f, 0.0f, 0.0f);<br /> glVertex3f(fLeft, fTop, -far);</p> <p>//far<br /> glVertex3f(fLeft, fBottom, -far);<br /> glVertex3f(fRight, fBottom, -far);</p> <p>glVertex3f(fRight, fTop, -far);<br /> glVertex3f(fLeft, fTop, -far);</p> <p>glVertex3f(fRight, fTop, -far);<br /> glVertex3f(fRight, fBottom, -far);</p> <p>glVertex3f(fLeft, fTop, -far);<br /> glVertex3f(fLeft, fBottom, -far);</p> <p>//near<br /> glVertex3f(nLeft, nBottom, -near);<br /> glVertex3f(nRight, nBottom, -near);</p> <p>glVertex3f(nRight, nTop, -near);<br /> glVertex3f(nLeft, nTop, -near);</p> <p>glVertex3f(nLeft, nTop, -near);<br /> glVertex3f(nLeft, nBottom, -near);</p> <p>glVertex3f(nRight, nTop, -near);<br /> glVertex3f(nRight, nBottom, -near);</p> <p>glEnd();<br /> glLineWidth(1);<br /> glPopMatrix();<br /> }<br /> </pre></p> OpenGL - FreeGlut Multiple Window Callbacks and C++ (OOP) 2009-12-12T18:15:18+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/2009/12/12/opengl-freeglut-multiple-window-callbacks-and-c-oop <p>Using glut with cpp can be difficult in some cases for example because of the glut callback specification. You can&#8217;t specify a callback to a object methods due to c limitations. One workaround is to use singletons as described here: <br /> <a href="http://www.uni-koblenz.de/~mgoi/?p=56">http://www.uni-koblenz.de/~mgoi/?p=56</a>. Another way to cope this issue is to use the glutGetWindow method. This method can be used within a static callback target method to determine which window should be updated etc. In my example i created a window class which is used to create and handle windows. Outside of this class i just created some wrapper callback methods which redirect the desired call to my object methods. <a id="more"></a><a id="more-437"></a></p> href="#fn3">3</a></sup>;</p> <p>void display(void) {<br /> int winId = glutGetWindow();<br /> //printf(&quot;win%i\n&quot;, winId &#8211; 1);<br /> windows[winId &#8211; 1]-&gt;display();<br /> }</p> 1]-&gt;refresh();<br /> }</p> <p>/**</p> <ul> <li>Keyboard function works for all windows.<br /> */<br /> void keyboard(unsigned char key, int x, int y) {<br /> if (key == 27)<br /> exit(0);<br /> }</li> </ul> <p>void idle() {<br /> for (int i = 0; i &lt; 3; i++) {<br /> windows[i]-&gt;idle();<br /> }<br /> }</p> <p>int main(int argc, char *argv[]) {<br /> glutInit(&amp;argc, argv);<br /> glutInitDisplayMode(GLUT_DOUBLE | GLUT_RGB);</p> <p>windows<sup class="footnote" id="fnr0"><a href="#fn0">0</a></sup> = new window(&quot;Window 0&quot;, <span class="caps">GAP</span>, <span glutMainLoop();<br /> }<br /> </pre></notextile></p> <p><strong>window.h</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax escaped c"><br /> #include &quot;window.h&quot;<br /> #include &lt;GL/glut.h&gt;<br /> #include &lt;GL/glu.h&gt;</p> <p>#define WIN_SIZE 200<br /> #define F_SIZE 200</p> <p>double angle = 0;</p> <p>window::window(string name, int posX, int posY) {<br /> this-&gt;_name = name;</p> Multiple Window & Events Example 2009-12-09T20:16:43+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/2009/12/09/xlib-multiple-window-events-example <p>This small example shows how to use events with xlib windows. After you created your windows you can check events of both of them. I tried to use threads for each displayWin* method to show them parallel and check within both the events. That did not work. What will work is shown in the example.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-434"></a></p> <p>See also <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xlib">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xlib</a>.</p> <pre class="syntax escaped c"> #include &lt;X11/X.h&gt; #include &lt;X11/Xlib.h&gt; #include &lt;unistd.h&gt; #include &lt;stdio.h&gt; Display *display; Window winA; Window winB; Window rootwindow; unsigned long white_pixel, black_pixel; void checkEvents() { XEvent xev; XWindowAttributes gwa; while (1) { printf(&quot;Next Iteration\n&quot;); // alternativly you can get the event of a determined window //XWindowEvent(display, winA, PointerMotionMask, &amp;xev); // the next call will lock until an event was received. XNextEvent(display, &amp;xev); switch (xev.type) { case Expose: { XGetWindowAttributes(display, winA, &amp;gwa); printf(&quot;Exposed Window\n&quot;); break; } case MotionNotify: { int MouseX = xev.xmotion.x; int MouseY = xev.xmotion.y; if (xev.xclient.window == winA) { printf(&quot;MouseA %i , %i\n&quot;, MouseX, MouseY); } else { printf(&quot;MouseB %i , %i\n&quot;, MouseX, MouseY); } break; } case ButtonPressMask: { printf(&quot;ButtonPressed - Destroying window\n&quot;); if (xev.xclient.window == winA) { XDestroyWindow(display, winA); } else { XDestroyWindow(display, winB); } break; } case KeyPress: { printf(&quot;Stopping event loop\n&quot;); return; } } } } void displayWinA() { printf(&quot;Creating window A\n&quot;); winA = XCreateSimpleWindow(display, rootwindow, 220, 220, 200, 200, 5, black_pixel, white_pixel); // name the window (titlebar) XStoreName(display, winA, &quot;Window A&quot;); // since we used XCreateSimpleWindow we need to enable event listening for this window XSelectInput(display, winA, StructureNotifyMask | ExposureMask | KeyPressMask | ButtonPressMask | PointerMotionMask); // map the window (make it visible) XMapWindow(display, winA); } void displayWinB() { printf(&quot;Creating window B\n&quot;); winB = XCreateSimpleWindow(display, rootwindow, 0, 0, 100, 100, 1, 0, 0); XStoreName(display, winB, &quot;Window B&quot;); XSelectInput(display, winB, StructureNotifyMask | ExposureMask | KeyPressMask | ButtonPressMask | PointerMotionMask); XMapWindow(display, winB); } int main(void) { int screen; display = XOpenDisplay(NULL); screen = DefaultScreen(display); white_pixel = WhitePixel (display, screen); black_pixel = BlackPixel (display, screen); rootwindow = RootWindow(display,screen); displayWinA(); displayWinB(); checkEvents(); XFlush(display); XDestroyWindow(display, winA); XDestroyWindow(display, winB); XCloseDisplay(display); return (0); } </pre> Minimal Google Docs Java Client objects were introduced with OpenGL 3.1. The following example is an adapted form of the <span class="caps">UBO</span> example from the <span class="caps">UBO</span> spec:<br /> <a href="http://www.opengl.org/registry/specs/ARB/uniform_buffer_object.txt">http://www.opengl.org/registry/specs/<span class="caps">ARB</span>/uniform_buffer_object.txt</a></p> <p>This example contains workarounds for an fglrx linux driver issue. The libGL.so of <span class="caps">ATI</span> (shipped with fglrx) does not export the correct amount of function symbols. Therefor you can&#8217;t use the functions that were defined within the glext.h header files. To workaround this issue i had to use glXGetProcAddress to determine the function address within the libGL.so. The address is used to create a function pointer and therefor use the function as usual.</p> <p>Uniform Buffer Objects allow fast exchange of uniform values because they were backed up by a buffer object. As far as i know <span class="caps">DMA</span> is used to transfer the data directly from your system memory into the <span class="caps">GPU</span> memory.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-427"></a><br /> This example requires <a href="http://freeglut.sourceforge.net/">freeglut 2.6.0</a> to initiate a opengl 3 context via glut. Please note that your driver must support UBO&#8217;s ( GL_ARB_uniform_buffer_object ).</p> <p><strong>GL3_UBO_Example.cpp:</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> #include <stdio.h><br /> #include &lt;GL/glx.h&gt;<br /> #include &#8220;GL/glext.h&#8221;<br /> #include &#8220;textfile.h&#8221;</p> <p>char *VertexShaderSource, *FragmentShaderSource;</p> <p>#define GLX_CONTEXT_MAJOR_VERSION_ARB 0&#215;2091<br /> #define GLX_CONTEXT_MINOR_VERSION_ARB 0&#215;2092</p> <p>typedef GLXContext (<strong>glXCreateContextAttribsARBProc)(Display</strong>, GLXFBConfig,<br /> GLXContext, Bool, const int*);<br /> #define glXGetProcAddress(x) (<strong>glXGetProcAddressARB)((const GLubyte</strong>)x)</p> <p>// mouse controls<br /> int mouse_old_x, mouse_old_y;<br /> int mouse_buttons = 0;<br /> float rotate_x = 0.0, rotate_y = 0.0;<br /> float translate_z = -2.0;</p> <p><span class="caps">PFNGLGETUNIFORMBLOCKINDEXPROC</span> mglGetUniformBlockIndex = <span class="caps">NULL</span>;<br /> <span class="caps">PFNGLGETACTIVEUNIFORMBLOCKIVPROC</span> mglGetActiveUniformBlockiv = <span class="caps">NULL</span>;<br /> <span class="caps">PFNGLBINDBUFFERBASEPROC</span> mglBindBufferBase = <span class="caps">NULL</span>;<br /> <span class="caps">PFNGLGETUNIFORMINDICESPROC</span> mglGetUniformIndices = <span = glGetError(); \<br /> exit(-1); \<br /> } \<br /> }</p> <p>// globals<br /> int initialized = 0;<br /> unsigned int window_width = 640;<br /> unsigned int window_height = 480;</p> <p>float delta = 0.01;<br /> GLfloat wf, hf;</p> <p>//uniform names<br /> const GLchar* names[] = { &#8220;SurfaceColor&#8221;, &#8220;WarmColor&#8221;, &#8220;CoolColor&#8221;,<br /> &#8220;DiffuseWarm&#8221;, &#8220;DiffuseCool&#8221; };<br /> GLuint buffer_id, uniformBlockIndex, uindex, vshad_id, fshad_id, prog_id;</p> <p>GLsizei uniformBlockSize;<br /> GLint singleSize;<br /> GLint offset;</p> <p>GLfloat initGlut(argc, argv);<br /> }<br /> </pre></p> <p><strong>shader.frag:</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> #extension GL_ARB_uniform_buffer_object : enable</p> <p>layout(std140) uniform ReflectVec;<br /> varying vec3 ViewVec;</p> <p>void main (void)<br /> {</p> vec3 kcool = min(CoolColor + DiffuseCool * SurfaceColor, 1.0); vec3 kwarm = min(WarmColor + DiffuseWarm * SurfaceColor, 1.0); vec3 kfinal = mix(kcool, kwarm, NdotL); vec3 nreflect = normalize(ReflectVec); vec3 nview = normalize(ViewVec); float spec = max(dot(nreflect, nview), 0.0); spec = pow(spec, 32.0); gl_FragColor = vec4 (min(kfinal + spec, 1.0), 1.0); <p>}<br /> </pre></p> <p><strong>shader.vert:</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> vec3 LightPosition = vec3(0.0, 10.0, 4.0);</p> <p>varying float * gl_Normal);<br /> vec3 lightVec = normalize(LightPosition &#8211; ecPos);<br /> ReflectVec = normalize(reflect(-lightVec, tnorm));<br /> ViewVec = normalize(-ecPos);<br /> NdotL = (dot(lightVec, tnorm) + 1.0) * 0.5;<br /> gl_Position = ftransform();<br /> }<br /> </pre></p> <p><strong>textfile.cpp:</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> #include <stdio.h><br /> #include <malloc.h><br /> Although the main purpose of this example is to show that ati cards do not support CLAMP_TO_BORDER when using TEXTURE_2D_ARRAY&#8217;s it might also be interessting for someone who want&#8217;s to know how to set a texture uniform (sampler2d) or (sampler2darray).</p> <p>The specification for texture arrays can be found here: <a href="http://developer.download.nvidia.com/opengl/specs/GL_EXT_texture_array.txt">http://developer.download.nvidia.com/opengl/specs/GL_EXT_texture_array.txt</a>. This extension is also supported by the newest ati cards. Screenshots were taken by using the example with an ati 4850 card and the latest drivers.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-396"></a></p> <p><b>Update &#8211; Note: </b> <br /> Compile with:<br /> <blockquote>g++ -Wall -lglut -lGL -lGLUW -o ExampleProg Simple_ATI_TEXTURE_2D_ARRAY_Example.cpp</blockquote><br /> Get sources and libs:<br /> <blockquote>apt-get install libglut3 libglut3-dev libglew1.5 libglew1.5-dev</blockquote></p> <p><b>Update:</b><br /> I just developed an workaround for this issue by adding clamp to border by myself to the shader:<br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> #extension GL_EXT_gpu_shader4 : enable</p> <p>uniform sampler2DArray base_texture;<br /> varying vec2 texCoord;<br /> void main()<br /> {</p> <p>vec4 borderColor =vec4(0.1,0.7,0.2,0.1);<br /> if(texCoord.s&lt;1 &amp;&amp; texCoord.s &gt;0 &amp;&amp; texCoord.t &lt;1 &amp;&amp; texCoord.t &gt;0)<br /> {<br /> borderColor = texture2DArray(base_texture, vec3(texCoord.st,1));<br /> }<br /> gl_FragColor = borderColor;</p> <p>}<br /> </pre></p> <p><strong><span class="caps">NOARRAY</span> &#8211; not definied</strong><br /> The example will use GL_TEXTURE_2D_ARRAY as source for texturing and a fragment shader that defines a sampler2DArray uniform:<br /> <img src="/images/opengl/GL_TEXTURE_2D_ARRAY_CLAMP_TO_BORDER-ATI.png" alt="GL_TEXTURE_2D_ARRAY_CLAMP_TO_BORDER-ATI" title="GL_TEXTURE_2D_ARRAY_CLAMP_TO_BORDER-ATI" width="412" height="327" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-397" /><br /> The texture is not clamped to the border even if the CLAMP_TO_BORDER attribute has been set.</p> <p><strong><span class="caps">NOARRAY</span> &#8211; definied</strong><br /> The example will use GL_TEXTURE_2D as source for texturing and a fragment shader that defines a sampler2D uniform:<br /> <img src="/images/opengl/GL_TEXTURE_2D_CLAMP_TO_BORDER-ATI.png" alt="GL_TEXTURE_2D_CLAMP_TO_BORDER-ATI" title="GL_TEXTURE_2D_CLAMP_TO_BORDER-ATI" width="392" height="292" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-398" /><br /> As you can see clamp to border works like a charm. I changed the border color to make the clamp effect clearly visible:</p> <p>Download the complete example sources: <a href="/downloads/opengl/opengl_texture_array_glsl_example.tgz">opengl_texture_array_glsl_example.tgz</a></p> <p><strong>shader_array.frag:</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> uniform vec3(texCoord.st*vec2(0.5,1.5), 0));<br /> gl_FragColor = color * base_color;</p> <p>}<br /> </pre></p> <p><strong>shader_simple.frag:</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> uniform sampler2D I had to do this because the projective center was in the middle of the texture. Without correction you get results like this one:</p> <p><img src="/images/opengl/texture_projection.png" alt="1" title="1" width="628" height="475" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-385" /></p> <p><img src="/images/opengl/texture_projection_2.png" alt="2" title="2" width="628" height="470" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-386" /></p> <p><strong>FragmentShader.glsl</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> uniform sampler2D projectionMap;<br /> varying vec4 projCoord;</p> <p>void main()<br /> {<br /> vec4 dividedCoord = projCoord / projCoord.w ;<br /> vec4 color = texture2D(projectionMap,dividedCoord.st+vec2(0.5,0.5) );<br /> gl_FragColor = color * gl_Color;<br /> }</p> <p></pre></p> <p><strong>VertexShader.glsl</strong><br /> <pre class="syntax c"><br /> varying vec4 projCoord;<br /> void main()<br /> {</p> <p>projCoord = gl_TextureMatrix<sup class="footnote" id="fnr1"><a href="#fn1">1</a></sup> * gl_Vertex;<br /> gl_Position = ftransform();<br /> gl_FrontColor = gl_Color;<br /> }<br /> </pre></p> GLSL shader to handle multiple projections onto the same surface 2009-08-17T23:20:56+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/technik/gfx/2009/08/17/glsl-shader-to-handle-multiple-projections-onto-the-same-surface <p>For my project <a href="http://www.jotschi.de/?page_id=320">Generating City Models By Using Panorama Images</a> i have to write a fragment shader that handles multiple projections onto the same surface. The shader must contain condition in which the projection should be handled. In my case i had to decide which projection source should be used to texture the desired model. <a id="more"></a><a id="more-363"></a><br /> I didn&#8217;t want to do alpha blending of each texture. I wanted that only the projection source will be used that would produce the best projection image. For a good projection the angle of which the projection &#8216;light&#8217; falls onto the surface must be very low. The second parameter is the distance.</p> <p>For example, imagine a scene with 20 projection sources. One source is very near the target surface but the angle in which the &#8216;light&#8217; falls onto the surface is very big so the texture produced by such a source wouldn&#8217;t be that good. Instead there is another projection source which&#8217;s projections angle is very low but the distance is larger than that of the near source. My shader will now pick the second projection source because the first does not match its condtions.</p> <p>Draft of my target shader:</p> <pre class="syntax c"> uniform int nTextures; uniform sampler2DArray textures; uniform vec3[] projectPos; varying vec3 glPos; varying vec3 normalVec; void main() { int currentTexture=0; float minAngle = 360.0f; float angleThreshold = 10.0f; // Select the texture with the lowest angle for(int i =0; i &lt;nTextures; i++){ float alpha = texture2DArray(textures,vec3(gl_TexCoord[0].xy, i)).a; if(alpha != 1.0f) { //TODO check calculation of projDirection vec3 projDirection =(projectPos-glPos); float angle = dot(normalVec,projDirection*-1); if(angle&lt;minAngle) { minAngle = angle; } } } float minDistance= -1.0f; // Select the texture with the lowest distance among those around the lowest angle for(i=0; i &lt;nTextures; i++){ float alpha = texture2DArray(textures,vec3(gl_TexCoord[0].xy, i)).a; // Condition 1: Must be visible if (alpha != 1.0f) { //TODO check calculation of projDirection vec3 projDirection =( projectPos-glPos); float angle = dot(normalVec,projDirection); // Condition 2: The angle must be between +-10.0f of the lowest angle if(angle&lt;(minAngle+angleThreshold) || angle&gt;(minAngle+angleThreshold)) { // TODO check calculation of distance between both points within R float dx = projectPos[i].x - glPos.x; float dy = projectPos[i].y - glPos.y; float dz = projectPos[i].z - glPos.z; float d = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy + dz * dz); // select the texture with the lowest distance if(d&lt;minDistance || minDistance ==-1.0f) { minDistance = d; currentTexture = i; } } } } gl_FragColor = texture2DArray(textures,vec3(gl_TexCoord[0].xy, currentTexture)); } </pre> <p>1. Maybe there is a better way to check if the given sample contains a texture value at the given texture coordinate than checking its alpha value.<br /> 2. I use a uniform to handle the size of the sampler2DArray textures array. Maybe you can extract that information within the shader<br /> 3. I use uniform vec3[] projectPos; to handle over the positions of the projection sources. Maybe this can be stored in the build in gl_LightSource array?</p> Debian testing and fglrx 8.632-1 ( Ati Driver Package 9.7 ) and linux-image-2.6.30-1-686-bigmem 2009-08-16T14:16:59+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2009/08/16/debian-testing-and-fglrx-8-632-1-ati-driver-package-9-7-and-linux-image-2-6-30-1-686-bigmem <p>Using my manual with the driver package ati-driver-installer-9-7-x86.&#215;86<em>64.run and kernel 2.6.30-1-686-bigmem will not work. http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2009/08/16/laggy-2d-fglrx-performance-debian-testing <p>I just made a dist upgrade and after starting X my 2D performance was awful. I checked /var/log/Xorg.0.log and found out that <span class="caps">DRI</span> had not been initialized. <a id="more"></a><a id="more-357"></a><br /> Reason for this was an update of libdrm2 to a newer version.</p> <p><code>Preparing to replace libdrm2 2.3.1-2 (using .../libdrm2_2.4.12-1_i386.deb) ... Unpacking replacement libdrm2 ... </code></p> <p>libdrm2_2.4.12-1 will not work with<br /> <code>fglrx-driver 8.62-1 Video driver for the ATI graphics accelerators </code></p> <p>Solution: <br /> Install the old libdrm2 version and restart X.<br /> <a href="http://packages.debian.org/lenny/libdrm2">Download: http://packages.debian.org/lenny/libdrm2</a></p> Generating City Models By Using Panorama Images 2009-07-13T00:03:19+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2009/07/13/generating-city-models-by-using-panorama-images <p><del datetime="2012-09-26T22:09:41+00:00">Currently i&#8217;m</del>Some time ago i was developing methods and software to transform panorama images into 3d models. The panorama image itself should be projected onto a generated 3d mesh. <br /> This would generate a textured 3d model which could be used as key for the development of different applications. In this article i will describe my approach and show some perspectives for some applications.<a id="more"></a><a id="more-320"></a><br /> A slightly similar approach is done by <a href="http://interactive.usc.edu/viewfinder/">viewfinder</a> which enables the user to position the image into a 3D context.</p> <h1>Project Goals</h1> <h2>Phase I goals:</h2> <ul> <li>Automatically creating a textured 3D city model.</li> </ul> <h2>Phase II goals:</h2> <ul> <li>Auto align any image that was taken within the area of the created city model.</li> </ul> <h2>Phase <span class="caps">III</span> goals:</h2> <ul> <li>Refine geometric data of the city model by using structure from motion techniques.</li> </ul> <h1>Project Description</h1> <p>By using <a href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/">openstreetmap &#8211; <span class="caps">OSM</span></a> data and basic computer vision edge detection of panorama images it is possible to find simple corrolating points between the panorama image and the openstreetmap data. The process is described below.</p> <p>Developing a software that is capabel of transforming information gathered from panoramic images and geo location based map data into a world model. Further this world model can be used to extrapolate the position of a viewer by corolating template images from the world model view and the image that was taken from the view.</p> <p><a href="http://interactive.usc.edu/viewfinder/index.html">Viewfinder</a></p> <p>httpv://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3b8ACCN3wSw<br /> This video shows the basic principle of projecting a panorama image onto 3d surfaces. This video is just a proof of concept that you can use openstreetmap data as a valid basis for the mesh generation. In my mind the accuracy is quite good.</p> <p><strong>Mesh generation:</strong><br /> <a href="/images/osm3d/unmapped.png"><img src="/images/osm3d/unmapped.png" alt="" title="Panorama Simple" width="500" class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-336" /></a><br /> This is the panorama source image.</p> <p><a href="/images/osm3d/mapped_lines.png"><img src="/images/osm3d/mapped_lines.png" alt="" title="Panorama Mapped Lines" width="500" class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-335" /></a><br /> By using the initial camera position and orientation of the panorama image we can align the openstreet map data. The arrows in the image indicates the direction in which the facing surface will be generated.</p> <p><a href="/images/osm3d/edges.png"><img src="/images/osm3d/edges.png" alt="" title="Extracted edges" width="500" class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-334" /></a><br /> The bottom end of the surface is defined by the openstreetmap data and the top end by the extracted contour.</p> <p><strong>Map generation:</strong><br /> To avoid generation of surfaces that can&#8217;t be seen by the viewer we just remove all these lines in the osm map data as described here. At first we generate the normal vectors for each line to determine if the (bottom) line will be part of a facing surface.</p> <p><a href="/images/osm3d/3.png"><img src="/images/osm3d/3.png" alt="" title="3" width="500" class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-332" /></a></p> <p>We remove all lines that do not belong to a facing surface by comparing the view vector with the normal vector.</p> <p><a href="/images/osm3d/2.png"><img src="/images/osm3d/2.png" alt="" title="2" width="500" class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-331" /></a></p> <p>After removing these lines we also remove the lines which are currently not visible by the viewer. This can be done by defining a 2d view volume. All lines that aren&#8217;t visible will be removed.</p> <p><a href="/images/osm3d/4.png"><img src="/images/osm3d/4.png" alt="" title="4" width="500" class="alignnone size-medium wp-image-333" /></a></p> <h1>Applications</h1> <p>Aligning any image with some parameters about its location precisely within this scene can open a variety of applications. Such as real time augmented reality applications. You can superimpose any content over an image or a video of the scene. And more specific: You could align your content to any surface the scene provides. Imagine arrows that point a direction along walls of a building.</p> <h1>Development</h1> <p>Currently i&#8217;m developing the applications in cpp using OpenCV and OpenSceneGraph (<span class="caps">OSG</span>).</p> <p>What i have done:<br /> <ul><br /> <li>Projective Textures using glsl shaders. 15.07.2009</li><br /> <li>Extracting horizon contour from images using OpenCV functions. &#8211; 19.07.2009</li><br /> <li>Creating a view volume that represents the actual view of the &#8216;projector&#8217; within the program. 06.07.2009</li><br /> <li>Align the extracted into the view volume of the program so that the contour will be superimposed over the viewed scene. &#8211; 22.07.2009</li><br /> <li>Transforming osm data coordinates to <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Transverse_Mercator_coordinate_system"><span class="caps">UTM</span>.</a> &#8211; 01.08.2009</li><br /> <li>Combining mesh creation &amp; osm data &amp; projection of image data within one program. &#8211; 03.08.2009</li><br /> <li>Extracting openstreetmap data via xml web api by using a adapted c library. &#8211; 03.08.2009</li><br /> <li>Developing a fast algorithm for generating a homogeneous polygon mesh between two lines. &#8211; 09.08.2009</li></p> </ul> <p>What needs to be done:<br /> <ul><br /> <li>Align a unknown image which was taken within the scene using <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scale-invariant_feature_transform">sift template matching</a> as key technology.</li><br /> <li>Handling multiple projection sources within one scene</li><br /> <li>Useing accelerometer data from wiimote to match the viewer orientation within the scene</li><br /> <li>Using <span class="caps">GPS</span> data to match the viewer position within the scene.</li><br /> <li>Refining the viewer attitude (position, field of view, orientation) by examine external image feed</li></p> </ul> <script src="http://www.gliffy.com/diagramEmbed.js" type="text/javascript"> </script><script type="text/javascript"> gliffy_did = "1785581"; embedGliffy(); </script><p><br/> Screenshots:<br /> <img src="/images/osm3d/pano1.png" alt="pano1" title="pano1" width="580" height="486" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-416" /><br /> <br/> Here you can see the generated mesh of the MQ using openstreetmap data. A projection is applied as texture to the model.</p> <p><br/><br/> <img src="/images/osm3d/pano2.png" alt="pano2" title="pano2" width="783" height="590" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-417" /><br /> <br/> Here you can see one projection face. A full projection will consists of four projection planes. One for each direction. As you can see the projection is divided into smaller parts. This must be done to achieve maximum image resolution of the projection since the maximum texture resolution is 2048&#215;2048.</p> <p><br/><br/> <img src="/images/osm3d/pano3.png" alt="pano3" title="pano3" width="770" height="664" class="alignnone size-full wp-image-418" /><br /> <br/> This is the projector view.</p> <p><br/><br/> <h1>Credits</h1><br /> The panorama image was taken by Jan Zarnikov. <a href="http://www.viewat.org/?i=en&sec=pn&id_pn=3878">Panorama at www.viewat.org</a></p> fglrx 9-6 to 9-11 Installation and Debian testing with 2.6.26-2-686-bigmem 2009-07-05T14:17:30+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/uncategorized/2009/07/05/fglrx-installation-and-debian-testing-with-2626-2-686-bigmem <p>My fglrx installation guide for Debian testing (squeez) with 2.6.26-2-686-bigmem.<br /> <a id="more"></a><a id="more-313"></a></p> <p>Update: I updated the post to meet fglrx 9-11 requirements.</p> <h2>Preperations:</h2> <p>1. Stop X</p> <p>2. Install additional packages you might need:<br /> <code>apt-get install module-assistant build-essential fakeroot dh-make debconf bzip2 wget libstdc++5 linux-headers-$(uname -r) </code></p> <p>3. Download ati-driver-installer-9-11-x86.&#215;86_64.run from <a href="http://www.amd.com">www.amd.com</a></p> <p>5. If you are using a source that supplies non-free packages you have to disable package acquisitions.</p> <p>Create the file /etc/apt/preferences with the following content:<br /> <blockquote>Package: fglrx-amdcccle <br /> Pin: version 8.62-1*<br /> Pin-Priority: 1001</p> <p>Package: fglrx-driver<br /> Pin: version 8.62-1*<br /> Pin-Priority: 1001</p> <p>Package: fglrx-driver-dev <br /> Pin: version 8.62-1*<br /> Pin-Priority: 1001</p> <p>Package: fglrx-kernel-src<br /> Pin: version 8.62-1*<br /> Pin-Priority: 1001</blockquote></p> <h2>Upgrade Steps:</h2> In case you want to upgrade your fglrx driver you need to take care of the following steps: <p>1. Unload fglrx module in case you are using it<br /> <code>modprobe -r fglrx </code></p> <p>2. Remove all fglrx packages. You might have to change the order of command due to dependencies between the packages.<br /> <code>// get a list of all fglrx packages sudo dpkg -l | grep fglrx sudo dpkg -P fglrx-driver sudo dpkg -P fglrx-kernel-$(uname -r) sudo dpkg -P fglrx-kernel-src sudo dpkg -P fglrx-amdcccle sudo dpkg -P fglrx-driver-dev // make sure everything is gone sudo dpkg -l | grep fglrx</code></p> <p>3. Restore files that might have been messed up by previous fglrx installations<br /> <code>apt-get --reinstall install libgl1-mesa-glx apt-get --reinstall install xserver-xorg-core</code></p> <p>4. Get rid of old ati configurations<br /> <code>sudo mv /etc/ati /tmp sudo mv /etc/X11/xorg.conf /tmp</code></p> <p><del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">5. Create new xorg.conf without ati specifications inside </del><br /> <del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">sudo dpkg-reconfigure xserver-xorg</del></p> <p><del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">6. Remove leftovers of previous installations:</del><br /> <del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">rm /usr/src/fglrx.tar.bz2</del><br /> <del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">rm /usr/src/<strong>fglrx</strong>.deb</del></p> <h2>Installation Steps:</h2> <p>1. Create the fglrx packages:<br /> <code>./ati-driver-installer-9-11-x86.x86_64.run --extract fglrx_9-11 cd fglrx_9-11 ln -s x740 x710 ./packages/Debian/ati-packager.sh --buildpkg testing </code></p> <p>2. Install the packages. You may have to change the order due to dependencies.<br /> <code>dpkg -i fglrx-driver_8.62-1_i386.deb dpkg -i fglrx-driver-dev_8.62-1_i386.deb dpkg -i fglrx-kernel-src_8.62-1_i386.deb dpkg -i fglrx-amdcccle_8.62-1_i386.deb</code></p> <p>Once you get the following error you can proceed with dpkg &#8212;force-all:<br /> <strong>trying to overwrite `/usr/lib/xorg/modules/extensions/libglx.so, which is also in package xserver-xorg-core</strong></p> <p>Finally i had to use the &#8212;force-all option to install the package. <br /> <code>dpkg --force-all -i fglrx-driver_8.62-1_i386.deb</code></p> <p><strong>This is a quite drastic step but otherwise the fglrx driver won&#8217;t install at all.</strong></p> <p>3. Build and install the fglrx kernel module. I had not to modify the sources in any way.<br /> <del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">module-assistant auto-install fglrx-kernel-src</del></p> <p>Update: This does not work any more. I do not know why. But here is the workaround:<br /> <code>module-assistant</p> <ol> <li><span class="caps">SELECT</span> &#8594; fglrx-kernel &#8594; <span class="caps">BUILD</span> / <span class="caps">INSTALL</span> #<br /> </code></li> </ol> <p><del datetime="2009-11-18T17:39:24+00:00">Please note that at this point no download should occure. If it does abort the installation. In that case the module-assistant downloaded the desired module from the non-free package tree. You can avoid this by removing non-free from your source.lst and rebuild the index via apt-get update.<br /> </del></p> <p>4. Load the module:<br /> <code>modprobe fglrx</code></p> <p>5. Make sure it was loaded. If it wasn&#8217;t loaded use dmesg to check what happed.<br /> <code>lsmod | grep fglrx</code></p> <p>6. Create the ati configuration.<br /> <code>aticonfig --initial</code></p> <p>7. Start X<br /> <code>startx</code><br /> Note:<br /> If you have trouble of setup a dual head environment without using Xinerama take a look the related post.</p> fglrx and Debian testing with 2.6.26-2-686-bigmem 2009-07-05T13:17:12+00:00 http://www.jotschi.de/fundgrube/2009/07/05/fglrx-and-debian-testing-with-2626-2-686-bigmem <p>Wuarg! Again <span class="caps">PAIN</span> with fglrx. Handover the texture to the fragment shader via uniform <strong>/<br /> osg::Uniform</strong> texUniform = new osg::Uniform(osg::Uniform::SAMPLER_2D,<br /> &#8220;projectionMap&#8221;);<br /> = osg::Vec3(0.0f, 0.0f, 324.0f);<br /> osg::Vec3 projectorDirection = osg::Vec3(osg::inDegrees(0.0f),<br /> osg::inDegrees(280.0f), osg::inDegrees(-460.0f));<br /> float projectorAngle = 110;<br /> osg::Vec3 up(0.0f, 0.0f, 1.0f);<br /> mat = osg::Matrixd::lookAt(projectorPos, projectorPos + projectorDirection,<br /> up) * osg::Matrixd::perspective(projectorAngle, 1.0, 0.1, 100);<br /> texMat&#8594;setMatrix(mat);<br /> stateset&#8594;setTextureAttributeAndModes(1, texMat, osg::StateAttribute::ON);</p> <p>stateset&#8594;setAttribute(projProg.get());<br /> return stateset;<br /> }<br /> osg::Node* createModel() {<br /> osg::Group* root = new osg::Group;</p> <p>/* Load the terrain which will be the receiver of out projection <strong>/<br /> osg::Node</strong> terr =
